  19. I was shopping for some jumbo hot rollers and ran across this set that I purchased a several months ago. I was curious about the review rating so I read them and am puzzled. I cannot share the same opinion as the negative reviewers. I find that the rollers heat extremely well and retain the heat. In fact, I begin using them when the indicator dot just begins to turn. Once I place the primary four large rollers in my hair I unplug the set to prevent overheating the curlers and causing damage to my hair since hot rollers should not be used everyday and can cause split ends. I have medium thick hair and a lot of it, it's shoulder length, no bangs and this set curls my hair beautifully! In fact, I have curly hair day one, and beautiful fluffy and nicely shaped hair the second day. I love the metal clips, but there is a trick to using them. You must put them in to keep tension on the curler - for instance, you put the clip in from the opposite direction that you rolled your hair and press the open end of the clip down to sit on your head. The clips do not mark or crease your hair as some other brands clips can. If you cannot use these rollers effectively, I would look at the products you are using in your hair. I notice if I use a silicone conditioner or hair serum ([[ASIN:B000VTRJMM CHI Silk Infusion - 6 oz.]], [[ASIN:B000P9DS4Q Frizz-Ease Extra Strength Serum, 1.69-Ounce]] or other similar products the curl falls out instantly. These products are great, but should only be used if you want to smooth and straighten your hair, they do not promote curling your hair.<br /><br />I purchased the [[ASIN:B000R87B1Q Conair SPC10X Super Clips, 10 Count]] that are suggested with this hot roller set, and while I do like them I prefer the metal clips that come with the set because they hold the curler tighter to your head. I do find the Super Clips effective for sectioning my hair for different styles, as well as sectioning my little sisters hair when I cut it, but not for the hot rollers, if you are rolling the curlers all the way to your head. If you have longer hair and just want to influence the ends they would be great. Don't get me wrong, they work, but they allow the curler to flop around on your head, and I like them tight to my head until they cool.<br /><br />UPDATE April 15, 2015 - My hair is long now, down to my elbows. I purchased the Conair Jumbo Flocked Rollers http://amzn.com/B007S69QAY and guess what? I like these better!! The smaller rollers in this review curl better even though I am way overloading the roller with my super long hair. I have re-tried the Hot Roller Super Clips and they still do not work for me, even with way more hair.   186. After reading many reviews on these rollers, I purchased them during a price drop. Unfortunately, they do not meet my expectations. I used to own an earlier Conair predecessor of these rollers in the 1980's, which contained liquid wax inside the core. Those rollers got very hot, and retained their heat. Unfortunately, this edition does not appear to have any heat conductor within the rollers; each roller is plastic through and through. So despite the fact that each roller sits on a metal heating rod, the rollers do not heat well or retain their heat. Why? Because plastic is not a good heat conductor. I had to heat these rollers for a full 25 minutes for them to get hot enough to perform, and even then, they produced only a mediocre curl. Too many small rollers were included with this set, so I would only recommend these rollers if you have short to medium-length hair. I would not recommend the rollers for long, thick, or course hair, as they don't get hot enough to manage those hair types. I am returning them for a refund, and will try a different variety.

They have performed extremely well for me.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I still have to use styling products in my hair to hold the curl for the day. The curlers never fell out of the base even when they were turned sideways. It's all in the packing. Yes, the pins went everywhere inside the base, but that could have been resolved if I had taken the time to just put them in a small zippered bag. I put all my other beauty products in zippered bags, so why not the pins for the curlers? As for having difficulty choosing the right pin, I just turned the pins upside-down in their compartment. It's just as easy to lay them out alongside the curlers, too. I thought these were minor difficulties. I bought the curlers to curl my hair without causing burns to my fingers or my scalp and they deliver.<br /><br />To add to another reviewer's bit of advice on securing the pins, I agree that the pins need to go in opposite the direction in which you are curling your hair. For most people, the ends of the pins will point either up or to your face, depending on where the curler is. I also found that if I \\"aim\\" for my head, instead of just trying to slide it in, then turn the pin upwards or toward my face when they touch my scalp and I know that they grabbed a bit of hair, that the curlers remain quite secure. I've also tried the Conair clips that are recommended and they are secure as well. I'm quite pleased with this purchase.<br /><br />Added note 7-2-14: Some reviewers said that the red dot heat indicator never turned white as it was supposed to. I always started rolling my hair about 5 minutes after I plugged in the set so the dot never got a chance to turn white. So I decided to test them. After 15 minutes, the dot was completely white and the rollers were actually so hot that I unplugged the set before I used them. Some of these sets just seem to have problems that I have not encountered with mine.

  283. I've tried several brands and makes with no luck. I finally found these at my local big box store for $13. I thought what the hay....it's $13 unlike the $40 paid on some cermamic rollers that only straightened my hair. I tried each set I bought at least a week, changing times heated to different style products,etc. None of them gave me one curl let alone a headful that would stay. So I thought for sure these would have the same issue. No on/off switch which is not a big deal to me as back in the ol' days most of them didn't. Rollers may look smaller than those from different sets but they do not give you Shirley Temple hair, despite some claims. I have YET to find hot roller sets that gives you the look of pin curls unless you are using hot rods. They come with pins and not clips. I prefer pins. There is a trick to using them. You want to curl to the root and use pin by placing it in the opposite side you curled. So if you are curling back, you push the pin down onto the curler and then forward or opposite direction the curler took. You are curling down, you push pin up. Make sure to have straight side of pin on the bottom of placement; it should the next to the scalp. While the teal colors are similar between the large and medium rollers this is not an issue. You have 2 locations where the pins are stored in the setter and you can easily separate the 2 to avoid confusion. Or separate them before you begin. There is no time suggestion on how long to preheat this setter. On average, these take 10-15 minutes for heat up. 15 minutes for optimum heating. 10 minutes works fine for me. These are plastic, yes. But they still retain heat. Just because you may not feel the scorching heat 10 minutes after placing them like some setters, doesn't mean they are not working. I leave them in for at least 20 minutes for most of the time 30 if I want a super bouncy curl. Curls release a bit after an hour to a nice full healthy curl. If you are not getting a curl, change products youare using or try using nothing. Anything silicone based will pull a curl out. Try using stuff that is volumizing or curl enhancing as products. Leave in oils like argon or coconut can also cause curls not to take. Think back in the day, most of the time our mothers only used a setting lotion on our hair for curls or just dampen our hair to pin curl or roll in sponge curlers.<br /><br />If you do not like the pins, you can always opt to buy clips to hold the rollers. I have found some at Sallys that work like Conair's but only a fraction of the price. By that I mean they are large enough to hold the curler but they do not have the long claws on the end.<br /><br />I actually went back to buy another set. Now I have 40 curlers and I have a wide range of options on how I would like to curl my hair now. I have as many as the large babyliss setter you can buy but for a quarter of what they cost. Give this setter a try. Have patience. They are worth it.

You MUST wait for the roller with the red dot to turn completely white before using them. Also, once you roll your hair, don't remove them too soon from your hair, like after only 15 minutes, because you want have a good curl - just sort of loose - but that might work for a causal affair, but won't hold up after an hour even with spray. The best for me has been to let the rollers heat for an least a hour before using them, then keep them in my hair for a least 30 minutes to have a curl that will last for hours. I have bone straight and semi thick hair, however, because everyone's hair will most likely respond differently you need to figure out what will work for you. Blessings!
